	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Special Relationship</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Special_Relationship_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Special Relationship (disambiguation)">Special Relationship (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="United Kingdom–United States relations">United Kingdom–United States relations</a></div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:-UNGA_(48791303991).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/-UNGA_%2848791303991%29.jpg/260px--UNGA_%2848791303991%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/-UNGA_%2848791303991%29.jpg/390px--UNGA_%2848791303991%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/-UNGA_%2848791303991%29.jpg/520px--UNGA_%2848791303991%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:-UNGA_(48791303991).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> (left) and U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> (right)</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Special Relationship</b> is an unofficial term often used to describe the political, diplomatic, cultural, economic, military, and historical <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="United Kingdom–United States relations">relations</a> between the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The term first came into popular usage after it was used in a 1946 speech by <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>. The two nations have been close allies during many conflicts in the 20th and 21st centuries, including <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>.
</p><p>Although both governments also have close relationships with many other nations, the level of cooperation between the UK and the U.S. in trade and commerce, military planning, execution of military operations, nuclear weapons technology, and intelligence sharing has been described as "unparalleled" among major <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">world powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wither_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wither-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The close relationships between British and American heads of government such as <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, as well as between <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and both <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> have been noted.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> At the diplomatic level, characteristics include recurring public representations of the relationship as “special”, frequent and high-profile political visits and extensive information exchange at the diplomatic working level.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The UK was the only European country to contribute troops to the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some critics deny the existence of a "special relationship", calling it a myth.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Former U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> considered <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> his "closest international partner" and said the UK would be at the "back of the queue" in any trade deal with the U.S. if it left the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, while accusing <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> of being "distracted by a range of other things" during the <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">2011 military intervention in Libya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph20161114_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph20161114-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>, President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> threatened to revoke <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a> loans due to Britain's invasion of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to recapture the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> rebuffed President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>'s request to employ British troops in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. Thatcher also privately opposed the <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">United States invasion of Grenada</a>, while Reagan unsuccessfully pressured against the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the election of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Premiership_of_Theresa_May" title="Premiership of Theresa May">British government</a> under Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> sought to establish "a new special relationship" with the <a href="/wiki/Trump_administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Trump administration">Trump administration</a>. Trump has claimed his relationship with Theresa May was "the highest level of special."<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although the "Special Relationship" between the U.K. and the U.S. was perhaps most memorably emphasized by Churchill, its existence, and even the term itself, had been recognized since the 19th century, not least by rival powers.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The governments of the United States and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> were enemies when foreign relations between them first began, after the American colonies declared their independence from British rule, triggering the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. Relations often continued to be strained through the mid-19th century, erupting into conflict during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> and again verging on war when Britain almost supported the rebel <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> in the early part of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. British leaders were constantly annoyed from the 1830s to the 1860s by what they saw as <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a>'s pandering to the democratic mob, as in the <a href="/wiki/Aroostook_War" title="Aroostook War">Aroostook War</a> in 1838–39 and the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_boundary_dispute" title="Oregon boundary dispute">Oregon boundary dispute</a> in 1844–46. However, British middle-class public opinion sensed a common "special relationship" between the two peoples based on their shared <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">language</a>, migrations, evangelical <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberalism</a>, and extensive private trade. This constituency rejected war, forcing <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> to appease the Americans. During the <a href="/wiki/Trent_Affair" title="Trent Affair">Trent Affair</a> of late 1861, London drew the line and Washington retreated.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Troops from the two nations had begun fighting side-by-side, sometimes spontaneously, in skirmishes overseas by <a href="/wiki/Taku_Forts#Second_Opium_War" title="Taku Forts">1859</a>, and the two <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">democracies</a> shared a common bond of sacrifice during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ramsay_MacDonald" title="Ramsay MacDonald">Ramsay MacDonald</a>'s visit to the U.S. in 1930 confirmed his own belief in the "special relationship", and for this reason he looked to the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty" title="Washington Naval Treaty">Washington Treaty</a> rather than a revival of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Japanese_alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Japanese alliance">Anglo–Japanese alliance</a> as the guarantee of peace in the Far East.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, as the historian <a href="/wiki/David_Reynolds_(English_historian)" class="mw-redirect" title="David Reynolds (English historian)">David Reynolds</a> observes: "For most of the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">period since 1919</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="United Kingdom–United States relations">Anglo-American relations</a> had been cool and often suspicious. United States 'betrayal' of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> was only the first in a series of US actions—over war debts, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty#Background" title="Washington Naval Treaty">naval rivalry</a>, the 1931–2 <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Manchurian crisis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Depression</a>—that convinced British leaders that the United States could not be relied on".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Equally, as President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>'s Secretary of State, <a href="/wiki/Dean_Acheson" title="Dean Acheson">Dean Acheson</a>, recalled: "Of course a unique relation existed between Britain and America—our common language and history ensured that. But unique did not mean affectionate. We had fought England as an enemy as often as we had fought by her side as an ally".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 210px; float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><caption>External video</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.c-span.org/video/?179761-1/franklin-winston"><i>Booknotes</i> interview with Jon Meacham on <i>Franklin and Winston: An Intimate Portrait of an Epic Friendship</i>, 15 February 2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/C-SPAN" title="C-SPAN">C-SPAN</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Churchillian_emphasis">Churchillian emphasis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Churchillian emphasis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britannialion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Britannialion.jpg/200px-Britannialion.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/Britannialion.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="223" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britannialion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A poster from <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> showing <a href="/wiki/Britannia_(emblem)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britannia (emblem)">Britannia</a> arm-in-arm with <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Sam" title="Uncle Sam">Uncle Sam</a>, symbolizing the Anglo–American alliance</div></div></div>
<p>The outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> provoked the rapid emergence of an unambiguously positive relationship between the two nations. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">fall of France</a> in 1940 has been described as a decisive event in <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>, leading the Special Relationship to displace the <a href="/wiki/Entente_Cordiale" title="Entente Cordiale">Entente Cordiale</a> as the pivot of the international system.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> During the war, one observer noted that "Great Britain and the United States integrated their military efforts to a degree unprecedented among major allies in the history of warfare".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> "Each time I must choose between you and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Roosevelt</a>", Churchill shouted at General <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Free_French" class="mw-redirect" title="Free French">Free French</a>, in 1945, "I shall choose Roosevelt".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Between 1939 and 1945, Churchill and Roosevelt exchanged 1,700 letters and telegrams and met 11 times. Churchill estimated that they had 120 days of close personal contact.<sup id="cite_ref-gunther1950_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gunther1950-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> During one meeting, Roosevelt was wheeled to Churchill's room while Churchill was taking a shower. The confused Roosevelt wanted to leave but Churchill urged him to remain: "British Prime Minister has nothing to cover from US President."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Churchill's <a href="/wiki/Lady_Randolph_Churchill" title="Lady Randolph Churchill">mother</a> was a U.S. citizen, and he keenly felt the links between the two English-speaking peoples. He first used the term "special relationship" on 16 February 1944, when he said it was his "deepest conviction that unless Britain and the United States are joined in a special relationship… another destructive war will come to pass".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He used it again in 1945 to describe not the Anglo–American relationship alone, but the U.K.'s relationship with both the U.S. and <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Canada–United Kingdom relations">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Special_relationship_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Special_relationship-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The New York <i>Times Herald</i> quoted Churchill in November 1945:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We should not abandon our special relationship with the United States and Canada about the atomic bomb and we should aid the United States to guard this weapon as a sacred trust for the maintenance of peace."<sup id="cite_ref-Special_relationship_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Special_relationship-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Churchill used the phrase again a year later, at the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, this time to note the special relationship between the U.S. on the one hand, and the <a href="/wiki/Anglosphere" title="Anglosphere">English-speaking nations</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">British Commonwealth</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Empire</a> under the leadership of the U.K. on the other. The occasion was his "Sinews of Peace Address", delivered in <a href="/wiki/Fulton,_Missouri" title="Fulton, Missouri">Fulton, Missouri</a>, on 5 March 1946:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Neither the sure prevention of war, nor the continuous rise of world organization will be gained without what I have called the fraternal association of the English-speaking peoples ...a <b>special relationship</b> between the British Commonwealth and Empire and the United States. Fraternal association requires not only the growing friendship and mutual understanding between our two vast but kindred systems of society, but the continuance of the intimate relationship between our military advisers, leading to common study of potential dangers, the similarity of weapons and manuals of instructions, and to the interchange of officers and cadets at technical colleges. It should carry with it the continuance of the present facilities for mutual security by the joint use of all Naval and Air Force bases in the possession of either country all over the world.
</p><p>There is however an important question we must ask ourselves. Would a special relationship between the United States and the British Commonwealth be inconsistent with our over-riding loyalties to the World Organisation? I reply that, on the contrary, it is probably the only means by which that organisation will achieve its full stature and strength.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>In the opinion of one international relations specialist: "the United Kingdom's success in obtaining US commitment to cooperation in the <a href="/wiki/Post-war" title="Post-war">postwar</a> world was a major triumph, given the isolation of the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A senior British diplomat in Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brimelow,_Baron_Brimelow" title="Thomas Brimelow, Baron Brimelow">Thomas Brimelow</a>, admitted: "The one quality which most disquiets the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> government is the ability which they attribute to us to get others to do our fighting for us ... they respect not us, but our ability to collect friends".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Conversely, "the success or failure of United States foreign economic peace aims depended almost entirely on its ability to win or extract the co-operation of Great Britain".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Reflecting on the symbiosis, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> in 1982 declared: "The Anglo-American relationship has done more for the defence and future of freedom than any other alliance in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg/220px-Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg/330px-Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg/440px-Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Pace_and_Jock_Stirrup_-_Oct_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Meeting of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff">Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff</a> and the British <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Defence_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the Defence Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Defence Staff</a> in 2006</div></div></div>
<p>While most government officials on both sides have supported the Special Relationship, there have been sharp critics. British journalist <a href="/wiki/Guy_Arnold" title="Guy Arnold">Guy Arnold</a> (b. 1932) denounced it in 2014 as a "sickness in the body politic of Britain that needs to be flushed out". Instead Arnold calls for closer relationships with Europe and Russia so as to rid "itself of the US incubus."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_cooperation">Military cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Military cooperation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg/220px-UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg/330px-UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg/440px-UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UnionJackandOldGlory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The flags of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States" title="Flag of the United States">United States</a> at a World War II memorial in Upper Benefield, England</div></div></div>
<p>The intense level of military co-operation between the UK and US began with the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Combined Chiefs of Staff">Combined Chiefs of Staff</a> in December 1941, a military command with authority over all US and British operations. Following the end of the Second World War the joint command structure was disbanded, but close military cooperation between the nations resumed in the early 1950s with the start of the Cold War.<sup id="cite_ref-wither_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wither-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shared_military_bases">Shared military bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Shared military bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the Second World War and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a>, the US has maintained substantial forces on Great Britain. In July 1948, the first American deployment began with the stationing of <a href="/wiki/B-29_Superfortress" class="mw-redirect" title="B-29 Superfortress">B-29 bombers</a>. Currently, an important base is the <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> facility <a href="/wiki/RAF_Fylingdales" title="RAF Fylingdales">RAF Fylingdales</a>, part of the US <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_Missile_Early_Warning_System" title="Ballistic Missile Early Warning System">Ballistic Missile Early Warning System</a>, although this base is operated under British command and has only one <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">USAF</a> representative for largely administrative reasons. Several bases with a significant US presence include <a href="/wiki/RAF_Menwith_Hill" title="RAF Menwith Hill">RAF Menwith Hill</a> (only a short distance from RAF Fylingdales), <a href="/wiki/RAF_Lakenheath" title="RAF Lakenheath">RAF Lakenheath</a>, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Mildenhall" title="RAF Mildenhall">RAF Mildenhall</a> (scheduled to close in 2024), <a href="/wiki/RAF_Fairford" title="RAF Fairford">RAF Fairford</a> (the only base for US strategic bombers in Europe), <a href="/wiki/RAF_Croughton" title="RAF Croughton">RAF Croughton</a> (not an air base but a military communications hub) and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Welford" title="RAF Welford">RAF Welford</a> (an ammunition storage depot).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the end of the Cold War, which was the main rationale for their presence, the number of US facilities in the UK has been reduced in number in line with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">US military</a> worldwide. Despite this, these bases have been used extensively in support of various <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> and offensive operations of the 1990s and early 21st century.
</p><p>The two nations also jointly operate on the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British</a> military facilities of <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> and on <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">Ascension Island</a>, a dependency of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a> in the Atlantic Ocean. The US Navy also makes occasional use of British naval bases at <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> and the US Air Force uses <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a> on <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, mainly for reconnaissance flights.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_weapons_development">Nuclear weapons development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nuclear weapons development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Agreement" title="Quebec Agreement">Quebec Agreement</a> of 1943 paved the way for the two countries to develop <a href="/wiki/Atomic_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic weapons">atomic weapons</a> side by side, the UK handing over vital documents from its own <a href="/wiki/Tube_Alloys" title="Tube Alloys">Tube Alloys</a> project and sending a delegation to assist in the work of the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>. The US later kept the results of the work to itself under the postwar <a href="/wiki/McMahon_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="McMahon Act">McMahon Act</a>, but after the UK developed its own thermonuclear weapons, the US agreed to supply delivery systems, designs and nuclear material for British warheads through the <a href="/wiki/1958_US-UK_Mutual_Defence_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="1958 US-UK Mutual Defence Agreement">1958 US-UK Mutual Defence Agreement</a>.
</p><p>The UK purchased first <a href="/wiki/UK_Polaris_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Polaris programme">Polaris</a> and then the US <a href="/wiki/Trident_nuclear_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="Trident nuclear programme">Trident</a> system which remains in use. The 1958 agreement gave the UK access to the facilities at the <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Test_Site" title="Nevada Test Site">Nevada Test Site</a>, and from 1963 it conducted a total of 21 underground tests there before the cessation of testing in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The agreement under which this partnership operates was updated in 2004; <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Nuclear_Disarmament" title="Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament">anti-nuclear activists</a> claimed renewal may breach the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. and the U.K. jointly conducted <a href="/wiki/Critical_mass" title="Critical mass">subcritical</a> nuclear experiments in 2002 and 2006, to determine the effectiveness of existing stocks, as permitted under the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty" title="Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty">Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_procurement">Military procurement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Military procurement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Reagan_administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Reagan administration">Reagan administration</a> offered Britain the opportunity to purchase the <a href="/wiki/F-117_Nighthawk" class="mw-redirect" title="F-117 Nighthawk">F-117 Nighthawk</a> stealth aircraft while a <a href="/wiki/Black_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Black program">black program</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rogoway20170103_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rogoway20170103-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The U.K. is the only collaborative, or Level One, international partner in the largest US aircraft procurement project in history, the <a href="/wiki/F-35_Lightning_II" class="mw-redirect" title="F-35 Lightning II">F-35 Lightning II</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The U.K. was involved in writing the specification and selection and its largest defense <a href="/wiki/Military_contractor" class="mw-redirect" title="Military contractor">contractor</a>, <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a> is a partner of the American prime contractor <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>. BAE Systems is also the largest foreign supplier to the US Defense Department and has been permitted to buy important US defense companies such as <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_Aerospace_Electronic_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed Martin Aerospace Electronic Systems">Lockheed Martin Aerospace Electronic Systems</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Defense" title="United Defense">United Defense</a>.
</p><p>
The US operates several British designs including <a href="/wiki/Chobham_Armour" class="mw-redirect" title="Chobham Armour">Chobham Armour</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Harrier_GR9" class="mw-redirect" title="Harrier GR9">Harrier GR9</a>/<a href="/wiki/AV-8B_Harrier_II" class="mw-redirect" title="AV-8B Harrier II">AV-8B Harrier II</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">US Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/T-45_Goshawk" class="mw-redirect" title="T-45 Goshawk">T-45 Goshawk</a>. The UK also operates several American designs, including the <a href="/wiki/FGM-148_Javelin" title="FGM-148 Javelin">Javelin anti-tank missile</a>, <a href="/wiki/M270_Multiple_Launch_Rocket_System" title="M270 Multiple Launch Rocket System">M270 rocket artillery</a>, the <a href="/wiki/AH-64_Apache" class="mw-redirect" title="AH-64 Apache">Apache gunship</a>, <a href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130 Hercules">C-130 Hercules</a> and <a href="/wiki/C-17_Globemaster" class="mw-redirect" title="C-17 Globemaster">C-17 Globemaster</a> transport aircraft.</p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_areas_of_cooperation">Other areas of cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other areas of cooperation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intelligence_sharing">Intelligence sharing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Intelligence sharing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg/220px-Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg/330px-Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg/440px-Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Menwith-hill-radomes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/RAF_Menwith_Hill" title="RAF Menwith Hill">RAF Menwith Hill</a> near <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a>, England, which provides communications and intelligence support services to both the United Kingdom and the United States</div></div></div>
<p>A cornerstone of the Special Relationship is the collecting and sharing of intelligence. This originated during World War II with the sharing of code-breaking knowledge and led to the <a href="/wiki/1943_BRUSA_Agreement" title="1943 BRUSA Agreement">1943 BRUSA Agreement</a>, signed at <a href="/wiki/Bletchley_Park" title="Bletchley Park">Bletchley Park</a>. After World War II the common goal of monitoring and countering the threat of communism prompted the <a href="/wiki/UK-USA_Security_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="UK-USA Security Agreement">UK-USA Security Agreement</a> of 1948. This agreement brought together the <a href="/wiki/SIGINT" class="mw-redirect" title="SIGINT">SIGINT</a> organizations of the US, UK, Canada, Australia, and New Zealand and is still in place today (see: <a href="/wiki/Five_Eyes" title="Five Eyes">Five Eyes</a>). The head of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a> station in London attends each weekly meeting of the British <a href="/wiki/Joint_Intelligence_Committee_(United_Kingdom)" title="Joint Intelligence Committee (United Kingdom)">Joint Intelligence Committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One present-day example of such cooperation is the <a href="/wiki/UKUSA_Agreement" title="UKUSA Agreement">UKUSA Community</a>, comprising the U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a>, the U.K. <a href="/wiki/Government_Communications_Headquarters" title="Government Communications Headquarters">Government Communications Headquarters</a>, Australia's <a href="/wiki/Defence_Signals_Directorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Defence Signals Directorate">Defence Signals Directorate</a> and Canada's <a href="/wiki/Communications_Security_Establishment" title="Communications Security Establishment">Communications Security Establishment</a> collaborating on <a href="/wiki/ECHELON" title="ECHELON">ECHELON</a>, a global intelligence gathering system. Under classified bilateral accords, UKUSA members do not spy on each other.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/2006_transatlantic_aircraft_plot" title="2006 transatlantic aircraft plot">2006 transatlantic aircraft plot</a>, the CIA began to assist the <a href="/wiki/MI5" title="MI5">Security Service</a> (MI5) by running its own agent networks in the <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistanis" title="British Pakistanis">British Pakistani</a> community. Security sources estimate 40 per cent of CIA activity to prevent a terrorist attack in the US involves operations inside the UK.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> One intelligence official commented on the threat against the US from <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Islam in the United Kingdom">British Islamists</a>: "The fear is that something like this would not just kill people but cause a historic rift between the US and the UK".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_policy">Economic policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economic policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The U.S. is the largest source of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> to the U.K., and the U.K. is likewise the largest single foreign direct investor in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> British trade and <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">capital</a> have been important components of the American economy since its colonial inception. In trade and finance, the Special Relationship has been described as "well-balanced", with <a href="/wiki/City_of_London#Economy" title="City of London">London</a>'s "light-touch" regulation in recent years attracting a massive outflow of capital from <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Irwin_Seltzer_2006_p._36_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irwin_Seltzer_2006_p._36-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The key sectors for British exporters to the U.S. are aviation, <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commercial_property" title="Commercial property">commercial property</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemicals">chemicals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_machinery" class="mw-redirect" title="Heavy machinery">heavy machinery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>British ideas, classical and modern, have also exerted a profound influence on U.S. economic policy, most notably those of the historian <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a> on <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> and the economist <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">John Maynard Keynes</a> on <a href="/wiki/Keynesian_economics" title="Keynesian economics">counter-cyclical spending</a>, while the British government has adopted <a href="/wiki/Workfare" title="Workfare">workfare</a> reforms from the U.S. American and British investors share entrepreneurial attitudes towards the <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">housing market</a>, and the fashion and <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">music</a> industries of each country are major influences on their counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-Seltzer,_p._36_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seltzer,_p._36-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Trade ties have been strengthened by <a href="/wiki/Globalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Globalisation">globalisation</a>, while both governments agree on the need for currency reform in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and educational reform at home to increase their competitiveness against <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>'s developing <a href="/wiki/Service_industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Service industries">service industries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Seltzer,_p._36_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seltzer,_p._36-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Tuttle" title="Robert H. Tuttle">U.S. ambassador</a> suggested to British business leaders that the Special Relationship could be used "to promote <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">world trade</a> and limit <a href="/wiki/Environmental_damage" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental damage">environmental damage</a> as well as combating terrorism".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a press conference that made several references to the Special Relationship, U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, in London with U.K. Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">William Hague</a> on 9 September 2013, said:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We are not only each other's largest investors in each of our countries, one to the other, but the fact is that every day almost one million people go to work in the United States for British companies that are in the United States, just as more than one million people go to work here in Great Britain for U.S. companies that are here. So we are enormously tied together, obviously. And we are committed to making both the U.S.-UK and the U.S.-EU relationships even stronger drivers of our prosperity.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Essay-like plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-essay-like" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>is written like a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_publisher_of_original_thought" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">personal reflection, personal essay, or argumentative essay</a></b> that states a Wikipedia editor's personal feelings or presents an original argument about a topic.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit">help improve it</a> by rewriting it in an <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Information_style_and_tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">encyclopedic style</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Special Relationship has often depended on the personal relations between British prime ministers and U.S. presidents. The first example was the close relationship between Winston Churchill and Franklin Roosevelt, who were in fact distantly related.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Prior to their collaboration during World War II, Anglo–American relations had been somewhat frosty. President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">David Lloyd George</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris</a> had been the only previous leaders of the two nations to meet face-to-face,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> but had enjoyed nothing that could be described as a "special relationship", although Lloyd George's wartime <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Affairs" title="Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs">Foreign Secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Balfour" title="Arthur Balfour">Arthur Balfour</a>, got on well with Wilson during his time in the US and helped convince the previously skeptical president to enter World War I.
</p><p>Churchill spent much time and effort cultivating the relationship, which paid dividends for the war effort. Two great architects of the Special Relationship on a practical level were Field Marshal Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Dill" title="John Dill">John Dill</a> and General <a href="/wiki/George_Marshall" title="George Marshall">George Marshall</a>, whose excellent personal relations and senior positions (Roosevelt was especially close to Marshall), oiled the wheels of the alliance considerably.
</p><p>Major links were created during the war, such as the Combined Chiefs of Staff. Britain, previously somewhat the senior partner, had found herself the junior beginning in 1941. The diplomatic policy was thus two-pronged, encompassing strong personal support and equally forthright military and political aid. These two have always operated in tandem; that is to say, the best personal relationships between British prime ministers and American presidents have always been those based around shared goals. For example, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>'s government would not commit troops to <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam</a>, and Wilson and <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> did not get on especially well.
</p><p>Peaks in the Special Relationship include the bonds between <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a> (who like Churchill had an American mother) and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>; between <a href="/wiki/James_Callaghan" title="James Callaghan">James Callaghan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>, who were close personal friends despite their differences in personality; between <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>; and more recently between <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and both <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>. Nadirs have included <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>'s opposition to U.K. operations in <a href="/wiki/Suez" title="Suez">Suez</a> under <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a> and Harold Wilson's refusal to enter the war in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Churchill_and_Roosevelt_.28May_1940.E2.80.93April_1945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Churchill_and_Roosevelt_(May_1940–April_1945)">Churchill and Roosevelt (May 1940–April 1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Churchill and Roosevelt (May 1940–April 1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg/220px-Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg/330px-Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg/440px-Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="587" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prince_of_Wales-5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Churchill and Roosevelt aboard <a href="/wiki/HMS_Prince_of_Wales_(53)" title="HMS Prince of Wales (53)">HMS <i>Prince of Wales</i></a> in 1941</div></div></div>
<p>When Winston Churchill entered the office of Prime Minister, the UK had already entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Immediately at the start of Churchill's Prime Ministership, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dunkirk" title="Battle of Dunkirk">Battle of Dunkirk</a> took place.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before Churchill's premiership, President Roosevelt had secretively been in frequent correspondence with him. Their correspondence had begun in September 1939, at the very start of World War II. In these private communications, the two had been discussing ways in which the US might support Britain in their war effort.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> However, at the time when Winston Churchill assumed the office of Prime Minister, Roosevelt was nearing the end of his second term and making considerations of seeking election to an unprecedented third term<sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> (he would make no public pronouncements about this until <a href="/wiki/1940_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1940 Democratic National Convention">the Democratic National Convention that year</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-gunther1950_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gunther1950-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> From the American experience during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, Roosevelt judged that involvement in the Second World War was likely to be an inevitability. This was a key reason for Roosevelt's decision to break from tradition and seek a third term. Roosevelt desired to be President when the US would finally be drawn into entering the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> However, in order to win a third term, Roosevelt made the American people promises that he would keep them out of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 1940, upon Roosevelt's victory in the presidential election, Churchill sent him a congratulatory letter,
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I prayed for your success…we are entering a somber phase of what must inevitably be a protracted and broadening war.<sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Having promised the American public to avoid entering any foreign war, Roosevelt went as far as public opinion allowed in providing financial and military aid to Britain, France and China. In a December 1940 talk, dubbed the <i><a href="/wiki/Arsenal_of_Democracy" title="Arsenal of Democracy">Arsenal of Democracy Speech</a></i>, Roosevelt declared, "This is not a fireside chat on war.  It is a talk about national security". He went on to declare the importance of American support of Britain's war effort, framing it as a matter of national security for the U.S. As the American public opposed involvement in the conflict, Roosevelt sought to emphasize that it was critical to assist the British in order to prevent the conflict from reaching American shores. He aimed to paint the British war effort as beneficial to the US by arguing that they would contain the Nazi threat from spreading across the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>If Great Britain goes down, the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> will be in a position to bring enormous military and naval resources against <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">this hemisphere</a>... We are the Arsenal of Democracy. Our national policy is to keep war away from this country.<sup id="cite_ref-natpark1_51-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natpark1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Franklin D. Roosevelt, Fireside chat delivered on December 29, 1940</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlanticcharter2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Atlanticcharter2.png/140px-Atlanticcharter2.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Atlanticcharter2.png/210px-Atlanticcharter2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Atlanticcharter2.png/280px-Atlanticcharter2.png 2x" data-file-width="616" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlanticcharter2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Churchill's edited copy of the final draft of the Atlantic Charter</div></div></div>
<p>To assist the British war effort, Roosevelt enacted the <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> policy and drafted the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a> with Churchill.<sup id="cite_ref-timefdrc_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timefdrc-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The US ultimately joined the war effort in December 1941, under Roosevelt's leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt and Churchill had a relative fondness of one another. They connected on their shared passions for <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Distilled_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Distilled beverage">liquors</a>, and their mutual interest in history and <a href="/wiki/Battleships" class="mw-redirect" title="Battleships">battleships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timefdrc_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timefdrc-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Churchill later wrote, "I felt I was in contact with a very great man, who was also a warm-hearted friend, and the foremost champion of the high causes which we served."<sup id="cite_ref-timefdrc_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timefdrc-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One anecdote that has been told to illustrate the intimacy of Churchill and Roosevelt's bond alleges that once, while hosting Churchill at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>, Roosevelt stopped by the bedroom in which the Prime Minister was staying to converse with him. Churchill answered his door in a state of nudity, remarking, "You see, Mr. President, I have nothing to hide from you." The president is said to have taken this in good humor, later joking with an aide that Churchill was, "pink and white all over."<sup id="cite_ref-timefdrc_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timefdrc-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 1939 and 1945, Roosevelt and Churchill exchanged an estimated 1700 letters and telegrams and met with one another 11 times.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On Churchill's 60th birthday, Roosevelt wrote him, "It is fun to be in the same decade as you."<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Beginning under Roosevelt and Churchill, the U.S. and U.K. worked together closely to establish the <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Churchill_and_Truman_.28April.E2.80.93July_1945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Churchill_and_Truman_(April–July_1945)">Churchill and Truman (April–July 1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Churchill and Truman (April–July 1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference,_16_July_1945._BU8944_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference%2C_16_July_1945._BU8944_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference%2C_16_July_1945._BU8944_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference%2C_16_July_1945._BU8944_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference%2C_16_July_1945._BU8944_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference%2C_16_July_1945._BU8944_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference%2C_16_July_1945._BU8944_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1703" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Harry_Truman_and_Winston_Churchill_shake_hands_on_the_steps_of_Truman%27s_residence_during_the_Potsdam_conference,_16_July_1945._BU8944_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Truman shakes hands with Churchill on 16 July 1945 (the first day of the Potsdam Conference, and only ten days before Churchill lost the premiership upon the announcement of the results of the <a href="/wiki/1945_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1945 United Kingdom general election">1945 election)</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Roosevelt died in April 1945, shortly into his fourth term in office, and was succeeded by his vice president, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Truman" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Truman">Harry Truman</a>. Churchill and Truman likewise developed a strong relationship with one another. While he was saddened by the death of Roosevelt, Churchill was a strong supporter of Truman in his early presidency, calling him, "the type of leader the world needs when it needs him most." At the <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">Potsdam Conference</a>, Truman and Churchill, along with <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, made agreements for settling the boundaries of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Attlee_and_Truman_.28July_1945.E2.80.93October_1951.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Attlee_and_Truman_(July_1945–October_1951)">Attlee and Truman (July 1945–October 1951)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Attlee and Truman (July 1945–October 1951)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TrumanAttleeKing1945_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/TrumanAttleeKing1945_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-TrumanAttleeKing1945_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/TrumanAttleeKing1945_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-TrumanAttleeKing1945_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/TrumanAttleeKing1945_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="395" data-file-height="356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TrumanAttleeKing1945_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Truman meeting with Attlee during the Potsdam Conference</div></div></div>
<p>Four months into Truman's presidency, Churchill's party was handed a surprise defeat at the polls, and <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a> became Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-historytodaybrookshire_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historytodaybrookshire-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The deputy in Churchill's wartime coalition government, Attlee had been in the US at the time of Roosevelt's death, and thus had met with Truman immediately after he took office. The two of them had come to like one another.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> However, Attlee and Truman never became particularly close with one another. During their coinciding tenure as heads of government, they only met on three occasions. The two did not maintain regular correspondence. Their working relationship with each other, nonetheless, remained sturdy.<sup id="cite_ref-historytodaybrookshire_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historytodaybrookshire-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Attlee assumed the position of Prime Minister, negotiations had not yet been completed at the Potsdam Conference, which had begun on 17 July. Attlee took Churchill's place at the conference once he was named Prime Minister on 26 July. Therefore, Attlee's first sixteen days as Prime Minister were spent handling negotiations at the conference.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Attlee flew to Washington in December 1950 to support Truman in standing up against <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In 1951, Truman pressured Attlee not to intervene against <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh" title="Mohammad Mosaddegh">Mossadeq</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-charmley_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charmley-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In his time as Prime Minister, Attlee also managed to convince Truman to agree to greater nuclear cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Churchill_and_Truman_.28October_1951.E2.80.93January_1953.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Churchill_and_Truman_(October_1951–January_1953)">Churchill and Truman (October 1951–January 1953)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Churchill and Truman (October 1951–January 1953)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_(cropped2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_%28cropped2%29.jpg/220px-Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_%28cropped2%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_%28cropped2%29.jpg/330px-Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_%28cropped2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_%28cropped2%29.jpg/440px-Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_%28cropped2%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1345" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Winston_Churchill_flashing_his_%22V_for_Victory%22_sign_and_President_Truman_waving_outside_Blair_House_in..._-_NARA_-_200108_(cropped2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The two leaders standing outside <a href="/wiki/President%27s_Guest_House" title="President&#39;s Guest House">Blair House</a> in 1949</div></div></div>
<p>Churchill became Prime Minister again in October 1951. He had maintained his relationship with Truman during his six-year stint as <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Leader of the Opposition (United Kingdom)">Leader of the Opposition</a>. In 1946, on invitation from Truman, Churchill visited the U.S. to deliver a speech at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_College_(Missouri)" title="Westminster College (Missouri)">Westminster College</a> in Truman's home state of <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>. The speech, which would be remembered as the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain_speech" class="mw-redirect" title="Iron Curtain speech">"Iron Curtain" speech</a>, affected greater public attention to the schism that had developed between the Soviet Union and the rest of the Allied Powers. During this trip, Churchill lost a significant amount of cash in a poker game with Harry Truman and his advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In 1947, Churchill had written Truman an unheeded memo recommending that the US make a pre-emptive <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bomb">atomic bomb</a> strike on Moscow before the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> could acquire nuclear weapons themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Churchill and Eden visited Washington in January 1952. At the time, Truman's administration was supporting plans for a <a href="/wiki/European_Defence_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Defence Community">European Defence Community</a> in hopes that it would allow <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> to undergo rearmament, consequentially enabling the U.S. to decrease the number of American troops stationed in Germany. Churchill opposed the EDC, feeling that it could not work. He also asked, unsuccessfully, for the US to commit its forces to supporting Britain in Egypt and the Middle East. This had no appeal for Truman. Truman expected the British to assist the Americans in their fight against communist forces in <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korea</a>, but felt that supporting the British in the Middle East would be assisting them in their imperialist efforts, which would do nothing to thwart communism.<sup id="cite_ref-charmley_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charmley-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Truman opted not to seek re-election in 1952, and his presidency ended in January 1953.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Churchill_and_Eisenhower_.28January_1953.E2.80.93April_1955.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Churchill_and_Eisenhower_(January_1953–April_1955)">Churchill and Eisenhower (January 1953–April 1955)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Churchill and Eisenhower (January 1953–April 1955)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wc0279.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Wc0279.jpg/220px-Wc0279.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Wc0279.jpg/330px-Wc0279.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Wc0279.jpg/440px-Wc0279.jpg 2x" data-file-width="531" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wc0279.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eisenhower (center) sits between Churchill (left) and <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Montgomery" title="Bernard Montgomery">Bernard Montgomery</a> at a NATO conference in October 1951. Eisenhower would be elected president just over a year later.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> and Churchill were both familiar with one another, as they had both been significant leaders of the Allied effort during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Relations were strained, however, by Eisenhower's outrage over Churchill's half-baked attempt to set up a "parley at the summit" with Joseph Stalin.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Eden_and_Eisenhower_.28April_1955.E2.80.93January_1957.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Eden_and_Eisenhower_(April_1955–January_1957)">Eden and Eisenhower (April 1955–January 1957)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Eden and Eisenhower (April 1955–January 1957)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Similarly to his predecessor, Eden had worked closely with Eisenhower during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_48-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suez_Crisis">Suez Crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Suez Crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a></div>
<p>When Eden took office, <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a> built up Egyptian nationalism and threatened to take control of the vital <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. Eden in 1956 made a secret agreement with France and Israel to seize control of the canal. Eisenhower had repeatedly warned Eden that the US would not accept British military intervention. When the invasion came anyway, the US denounced it at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, and used financial power to force the British to completely withdraw. Britain lost its prestige and its powerful role in Mid-Eastern affairs, to be replaced by the Americans. Eden, in poor health, was forced to retire.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Macmillan_and_Eisenhower_.28January_1957.E2.80.93January_1961.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Macmillan_and_Eisenhower_(January_1957–January_1961)">Macmillan and Eisenhower (January 1957–January 1961)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Macmillan and Eisenhower (January 1957–January 1961)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
