<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg/220px-Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg/330px-Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg/440px-Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1239" data-file-height="831" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thatcher_and_Bush_-_1990_-_P14935-18A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Thatcher</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">Bush</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aspen,_Colorado" title="Aspen, Colorado">Aspen, Colorado</a> in August 1990</div></div></div>
<p>In his personal diary, <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> wrote that his first impression of Thatcher was she was principled but very difficult. Bush also wrote that Thatcher, "talks all the time when you're in a conversation. It's a one-way street."<sup id="cite_ref-destinyandpower_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destinyandpower-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite having developed a warm relation with Reagan, whom Bush had served under as vice president, Thatcher never developed a similar sense of camaraderie with Bush. At the time that Bush <a href="/wiki/1988_United_States_presidential_election" title="1988 United States presidential election">took office in 1989</a>, Thatcher was politically under siege by both political opposition, as well as from forces within her own party.<sup id="cite_ref-csmbush_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csmbush-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bush was anxious to manage the collapse of communist regimes in Eastern Europe in a manner that would produce order and stability. Bush therefore used a 1989 trip to Brussels to demonstrate the heightened attention that his administration planned to allocate towards <a href="/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Germany–United States relations">US-German relations</a>. Thus, rather than giving Thatcher the precedence which Prime Ministers of the United Kingdom were accustomed to receiving from US Presidents, he met with the president of the European Commission first, leaving Thatcher, "cooling her heels". This irritated Thatcher.<sup id="cite_ref-csmbush_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csmbush-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1989, after Bush proposed a reduction in US troops stationed in Europe, Thatcher lectured Bush on the importance of freedom. Bush came out of this encounter asking, "Why does she have any doubt that we feel this way on this issue?"<sup id="cite_ref-destinyandpower_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destinyandpower-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the midst of the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invasion of Kuwait</a>, Thatcher advised Bush that, "this is no time to go wobbly."<sup id="cite_ref-destinyandpower_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destinyandpower-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-csmbush_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csmbush-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Thatcher <a href="/wiki/1990_Conservative_Party_leadership_election" title="1990 Conservative Party leadership election">lost her premiership in November 1990</a>. However, to Bush's displeasure, she continued attempting to involve herself in diplomacy between the West and the Soviet Union. Bush took particular offence to a speech Thatcher gave after leaving office in which she claimed that she and Ronald Reagan were responsible for ending the Cold War. Thatcher gave this speech, which snubbed the contributions that others had made, before an audience that included a number of individuals who had contributed to the ending the Cold War, such as <a href="/wiki/Lech_Wa%C5%82%C4%99sa" title="Lech Wałęsa">Lech Wałęsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="Václav Havel">Václav Havel</a>. In reaction to this speech, <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a> sent Bush a note proclaiming that Thatcher was crazy.<sup id="cite_ref-destinyandpower_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destinyandpower-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Major_and_George_H.W._Bush_.28November_1990.E2.80.93January_1993.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_and_George_H.W._Bush_(November_1990–January_1993)">Major and George H.W. Bush (November 1990–January 1993)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Major and George H.W. Bush (November 1990–January 1993)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arcbushmaj.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Arcbushmaj.jpg/220px-Arcbushmaj.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Arcbushmaj.jpg/330px-Arcbushmaj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Arcbushmaj.jpg/440px-Arcbushmaj.jpg 2x" data-file-width="588" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arcbushmaj.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> (left) and President <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> (right) in June 1992</div></div></div>
<p>As had started becoming apparent in Thatcher's last few years of premiership, the Special Relationship had begun to wane for a time with the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, despite <a href="/wiki/Operation_Granby" title="Operation Granby">intensive co-operation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>. Thus, while it remained the case that "On almost all issues, Britain and the US are on the same side of the table. You cannot say that for other important allies such as France, Germany or Japan",<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> it was also acknowledged that "The disappearance of a powerful common threat, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, has allowed narrower disputes to emerge and given them greater weight."<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Major_and_Clinton_.28January_1993.E2.80.93May_1997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_and_Clinton_(January_1993–May_1997)">Major and Clinton (January 1993–May 1997)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Major and Clinton (January 1993–May 1997)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium,_1994.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium%2C_1994.jpg/220px-Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium%2C_1994.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium%2C_1994.jpg/330px-Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium%2C_1994.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium%2C_1994.jpg/440px-Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium%2C_1994.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1040" data-file-height="688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_and_John_Major_breakfast_meeting_the_White_House_Solarium,_1994.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> (left) and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> (right) hold a working breakfast at the White House in 1994.</div></div></div>
<p>Republican administrations had typically worked well with Conservative governments, and the new Democratic President Bill Clinton intended to maintain the Special Relationship. But he and Major did not prove compatible.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
The nuclear alliance was weakened when Clinton extended a moratorium on <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear testing">tests</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Test_Site" title="Nevada Test Site">Nevada desert</a> in 1993, and pressed Major to agree to the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty" title="Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty">Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The freeze was described by a British <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gascoyne-Cecil,_7th_Marquess_of_Salisbury" title="Robert Gascoyne-Cecil, 7th Marquess of Salisbury">defence minister</a> as "unfortunate and misguided", as it inhibited validation of the "safety, reliability and effectiveness" of fail-safe mechanisms on upgraded warheads for the <a href="/wiki/UK_Trident_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Trident programme">British Trident II</a> <a href="/wiki/UGM-133_Trident_II" title="UGM-133 Trident II">D5 missiles</a>, and potentially the development of a new deterrent for the 21st century, leading Major to consider a return to Pacific Ocean testing.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The Ministry of Defence turned to computer simulation.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A genuine crisis in transatlantic relations blew up over <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> London and Paris resisted relaxation of the UN <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War#Arms_Embargo" title="Bosnian War">arms embargo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> and discouraged U.S. <a href="/wiki/Lift_and_strike_(Bosnia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lift and strike (Bosnia)">escalation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> arguing that arming the <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Muslims</a> or bombing the <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Serbs of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Serbs</a> could worsen the bloodshed and endanger their <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force" title="United Nations Protection Force">peacekeepers</a> on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-Ian_Black_1993_p._22_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ian_Black_1993_p._22-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Warren_Christopher" title="Warren Christopher">Warren Christopher</a>'s campaign to lift the embargo was rebuffed by Major and President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="François Mitterrand">Mitterrand</a> in May 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> After the so-called '<a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> ambush' in June 1993, where Clinton "ganged up" with <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(1949%E2%80%93)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (1949–)">Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Kohl</a> to rally the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Community</a> against the peacekeeping states, Major was said to be contemplating the death of the Special Relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The following month the United States voted at the UN with <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">non-aligned countries</a> against Britain and France over lifting the embargo.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By October 1993, Warren Christopher was bristling that Washington policy makers had been too "<a href="/wiki/Eurocentrism" title="Eurocentrism">Eurocentric</a>", and declared that Western Europe was "no longer the <a href="/wiki/Hegemony#History" title="Hegemony">dominant area</a> of the world".<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. ambassador to London, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_G.H._Seitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Raymond G.H. Seitz">Raymond G.H. Seitz</a>, demurred, insisting it was far too early to put a "tombstone" over the Special Relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-Ian_Black_1993_p._22_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ian_Black_1993_p._22-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> A senior <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> official described Bosnia in the spring of 1995 as the worst crisis with the British and French since Suez.<sup id="cite_ref-Walker_p._21_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._21-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> By the summer, U.S. officials were doubting whether NATO had a future.<sup id="cite_ref-Walker_p._21_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._21-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The nadir had now been reached, and, along with <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">NATO enlargement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Croats" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnian Croats">Croatian</a> offensive in 1995 that opened the way for <a href="/wiki/1995_NATO_bombing_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="1995 NATO bombing of Bosnia and Herzegovina">NATO bombing</a>, the strengthening Clinton-Major relationship was later credited as one of three developments that saved the Western alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-Walker_p._21_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._21-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The president later acknowledged,
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>John Major carried a lot of water for me and for the alliance over Bosnia. I know he was under a lot of political pressure at home, but he never wavered. He was a truly decent guy who never let me down. We worked really well together, and I got to like him a lot.<sup id="cite_ref-Walker_p._21_158-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._21-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>A rift opened in a further area. In February 1994, Major refused to answer Clinton's telephone calls for days over his decision to grant <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn Féin">Sinn Féin</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams" title="Gerry Adams">Gerry Adams</a> a <a href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa (document)">visa</a> to visit the United States to agitate.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Adams was listed as a terrorist by <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reference1_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reference1-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. State Department, the CIA, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">U.S. Justice Department</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> all opposed the move on the grounds that it made the United States look "soft on terrorism" and "could do irreparable damage to the special relationship".<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Under pressure from <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>, the president hoped the visit would encourage the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">IRA</a> to renounce violence.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> While Adams offered nothing new, and violence escalated within weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> the president later claimed vindication after the IRA ceasefire of August 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> To the disappointment of the prime minister, Clinton lifted the ban on official contacts and received Adams at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> on <a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Patrick&#39;s Day">St. Patrick's Day</a> 1995, despite the fact the paramilitaries had not agreed to disarm.<sup id="cite_ref-Reference1_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reference1-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The rows over <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> and the Adams affair reportedly "provoked incandescent Clintonian rages".<sup id="cite_ref-Walker_p._21_158-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._21-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 1995, Clinton became only the second US president ever to address both <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Houses of Parliament</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Glory&#39;,_1995_p._8_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glory&#39;,_1995_p._8-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> but, by the end of Major's premiership, disenchantment with the Special Relationship had deepened to the point where the incoming British ambassador <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Meyer" title="Christopher Meyer">Christopher Meyer</a> banned the "hackneyed phrase" from the <a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_Kingdom_in_Washington,_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Embassy of the United Kingdom in Washington, D.C.">embassy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Blair_and_Clinton_.28May_1997.E2.80.93January_2001.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Blair_and_Clinton_(May_1997–January_2001)">Blair and Clinton (May 1997–January 2001)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Blair and Clinton (May 1997–January 2001)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_Blair.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Clinton_Blair.jpg/220px-Clinton_Blair.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cb/Clinton_Blair.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="278" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clinton_Blair.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> (left) and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> (right) at the Conference on Progressive Governance, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, in November 1999</div></div></div>
<p>The election of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1997 United Kingdom general election">1997</a> brought an opportunity to revive what Clinton called the two nations' "unique partnership". At his first meeting with his new partner, the president said: "Over the last fifty years our unbreakable alliance has helped to bring unparalleled peace and prosperity and security. It's an alliance based on shared values and common aspirations."<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The personal relationship was seen as especially close because the leaders were "kindred spirits" in their domestic agendas.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Third_Way" title="Third Way">Third Way</a>, a moderate <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a> position, was partly influenced by US <a href="/wiki/New_Democrats" title="New Democrats">New Democratic</a> thinking.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Co-operation in defence and communications still had the potential to embarrass Blair, however, as he strove to balance it with his own leadership role in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU).<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Enforcement of <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_no-fly_zones" title="Iraqi no-fly zones">Iraqi no-fly zones</a><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> and US bombing raids on <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> dismayed EU partners.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> As the leading international proponent of <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_intervention" title="Humanitarian intervention">humanitarian intervention</a>, the "hawkish" Blair "bullied" Clinton to back diplomacy with force in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> in 1999, pushing for deployment of <a href="/wiki/Ground_troops" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground troops">ground troops</a> to persuade the president "to do whatever was necessary" to win.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Blair_and_George_W._Bush_.28January_2001.E2.80.93June_2007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Blair_and_George_W._Bush_(January_2001–June_2007)">Blair and George W. Bush (January 2001–June 2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Blair and George W. Bush (January 2001–June 2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg/220px-Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg/330px-Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg/440px-Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg 2x" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush_and_Blair_at_Camp_David.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> (left) and President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> (right) at <a href="/wiki/Camp_David" title="Camp David">Camp David</a> in March 2003, during the build-up to the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a></div></div></div>
<p>The personal diplomacy of Blair and Clinton's successor, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">US president</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> in <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_presidential_election" title="2000 United States presidential election">2001</a>, further served to highlight the Special Relationship. Despite their political differences on non-strategic matters, their shared beliefs and responses to the international situation formed a commonality of purpose following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in New York and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> Blair, like Bush, was convinced of the importance of moving against the perceived threat to world peace and international order, famously pledging to stand "shoulder to shoulder" with Bush:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>This is not a battle between the United States of America and terrorism, but between the free and democratic world and terrorism. We therefore here in Britain stand shoulder to shoulder with our American friends in this hour of tragedy, and we, like them, will not rest until this evil is driven from our world.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Blair flew to Washington immediately after 9/11 to affirm British solidarity with the United States. In a speech to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>, nine days after the attacks, Bush declared "America has no truer friend than Great Britain."<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Blair, one of the few world leaders to attend a presidential speech to Congress as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_%22Lenny_Skutniks%22" class="mw-redirect" title="List of &quot;Lenny Skutniks&quot;">special guest of the First Lady</a>, received two standing ovations from members of Congress. Blair's presence at the presidential speech remains the only time in U.S. political history that a foreign leader was in attendance at an emergency joint session of the U.S. Congress, a testimony to the strength of the U.S.–U.K. alliance under the two leaders. Following that speech, Blair embarked on two months of diplomacy, rallying international support for military action. The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> calculated that, in total, the prime minister held 54 meetings with world leaders and travelled more than 40,000 miles (64,000&#160;km).
</p><p>Blair's leadership role in the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> helped him to sustain a strong relationship with Bush through to the end of his time as prime minister, but it was unpopular within his own party and lowered his public approval ratings. Some of the British Press called Blair "Bush's poodle."<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> It also alienated some of his European partners, including the leaders of France and Germany. Russian popular artist <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Nikolayevich_Zadornov" title="Mikhail Nikolayevich Zadornov">Mikhail Nikolayevich Zadornov</a> mused that "the position adopted by Britain towards America in the context of the Iraq War would be officially introduced into <a href="/wiki/Kama_Sutra" title="Kama Sutra">Kama Sutra</a>." Blair felt he could defend his close personal relationship with Bush by claiming it had brought progress in the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_peace_process" title="Israeli–Palestinian peace process">Middle East peace process</a>, aid for Africa and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate-change</a> diplomacy.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> However, it was not with Bush but with <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">California Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> that Blair ultimately succeeded in setting up a <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">carbon-trading market</a>, "creating a model other states will follow".<sup id="cite_ref-Irwin_Seltzer_2006_p._36_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irwin_Seltzer_2006_p._36-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 Lebanon War</a> also exposed some minor differences in attitudes over the Middle East. The strong support offered by Blair and the Bush administration to <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> was not wholeheartedly shared by the British cabinet or the British public. On 27 July, Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Beckett" title="Margaret Beckett">Margaret Beckett</a> criticised the United States for "ignoring procedure" when using <a href="/wiki/Prestwick_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestwick Airport">Prestwick Airport</a> as a stop-off point for delivering <a href="/wiki/Laser-guided_bomb" title="Laser-guided bomb">laser-guided bombs</a> to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Brown_and_George_W._Bush_.28June_2007.E2.80.93January_2009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brown_and_George_W._Bush_(June_2007–January_2009)">Brown and George W. Bush (June 2007–January 2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Brown and George W. Bush (June 2007–January 2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg/220px-20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg/330px-20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg/440px-20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="338" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20070730_Bush_Brown_Camp_David_shake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> (left) and President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> (right) at <a href="/wiki/Camp_David" title="Camp David">Camp David</a> in July 2007</div></div></div>
<p>Although British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> stated his support for the United States on assuming office in <a href="/wiki/2007_Labour_Party_(UK)_leadership_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Labour Party (UK) leadership election">2007</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> he appointed ministers to the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign Office</a> who had been critical of aspects of the relationship or of recent US policy.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Whitehall" title="Whitehall">Whitehall</a> source said: "It will be more businesslike now, with less emphasis on the meeting of personal visions you had with Bush and Blair."<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> British policy was that the relationship with the United States remained the United Kingdom's "most important bilateral relationship".<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Brown_and_Obama_.28January_2009.E2.80.93May_2010.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brown_and_Obama_(January_2009–May_2010)">Brown and Obama (January 2009–May 2010)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Brown and Obama (January 2009–May 2010)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg/220px-President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg/330px-President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg/440px-President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg 2x" data-file-width="479" data-file-height="318" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Barack_Obama_meets_Prime_Minister_Gordon_Brown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> (left) and President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> (right) in the <a href="/wiki/Oval_Office" title="Oval Office">Oval Office</a> in March 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Prior to his <a href="/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election" title="2008 United States presidential election">election as US president in 2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, suggesting that Blair and Britain had been let down by the Bush administration, declared: "We have a chance to recalibrate the relationship and for the United Kingdom to work with America as a full partner."<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On meeting Brown as president for the first time in March 2009, Obama reaffirmed that "Great Britain is one of our closest and strongest allies and there is a link and bond there that will not break... This notion that somehow there is any lessening of that special relationship is misguided... The relationship is not only special and strong but will only get stronger as time goes on."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Commentators, however, noted that the recurring use of "special partnership" by <a href="/wiki/White_House_Press_Secretary" title="White House Press Secretary">White House Press Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gibbs" title="Robert Gibbs">Robert Gibbs</a> could be signaling an effort to recast terms.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Special Relationship was also reported to be "strained" after a senior <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> official criticised a British decision to talk to the political wing of <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>, complaining that the United States had not been properly informed.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The protest came after the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration#Middle_East" title="Foreign policy of the Barack Obama administration">Obama administration</a> had said it was prepared to talk to <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> and at the same time as it was making overtures to <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> A senior <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Office">Foreign Office</a> official responded: "This should not have come as a shock to any official who might have been in the previous administration and is now in the current one."<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2009 the special relationship was reported to have "taken another hit"<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> after the British government was said to be "angry"<sup id="cite_ref-Leonard_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> over the failure of the US to seek its approval before negotiating with <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> over the resettlement to the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British overseas territory</a><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> of four ex-<a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Bay_detention_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Guantánamo Bay detention camp">Guantanamo Bay</a> inmates wanted by the People's Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> A Foreign Office spokesman said: 'It's something that we should have been consulted about.'<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Asked whether the men might be sent back to <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, he replied: "We are looking into all possible next steps."<sup id="cite_ref-Leonard_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The move prompted an urgent security assessment by the British government.<sup id="cite_ref-Churcher_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Churcher-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Shadow Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">William Hague</a> demanded an explanation from the incumbent, <a href="/wiki/David_Miliband" title="David Miliband">David Miliband</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Churcher_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Churcher-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> as comparisons were drawn with his previous embarrassment over the US use of Diego Garcia for extraordinary rendition without British knowledge,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> with one commentator describing the affair as "a wake-up call" and "the latest example of American governments ignoring Britain when it comes to US interests in British territories abroad".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2009, the Special Relationship was again reported to have "taken another blow" with the release on compassionate grounds of <a href="/wiki/Abdelbaset_al-Megrahi" title="Abdelbaset al-Megrahi">Abdelbaset al-Megrahi</a>, the man convicted of the 1988 <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Lockerbie Bombing</a>. U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> said "it was absolutely wrong to release Abdelbaset al-Megrahi", adding "We are still encouraging the Scottish authorities not to do so and hope they will not". Obama also commented that the release of al-Megrahi was a "mistake" and "highly objectionable".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2010, Hillary Clinton's support for <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>'s call for negotiations over the Falkland Islands triggered a series of diplomatic protests from Britain<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> and renewed public scepticism about the value of the Special Relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The British government rejected Clinton's offer of mediation after renewed tensions with Argentina were triggered by a British decision to drill for oil near the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The British government's long-standing position was that the Falklands were British territory, with all that this implied regarding the legitimacy of British commercial activities within its boundaries. British officials were therefore irritated by the implication that sovereignty was negotiable.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later that month, the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs_Select_Committee" title="Foreign Affairs Select Committee">Foreign Affairs Select Committee</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> suggested that the British government should be "less deferential" towards the United States and focus relations more on British interests.<sup id="cite_ref-notspecial2010_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notspecial2010-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-parl2010_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parl2010-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> According to Committee Chair <a href="/wiki/Mike_Gapes" title="Mike Gapes">Mike Gapes</a>, "The UK and US have a close and valuable relationship not only in terms of intelligence and security but also in terms of our profound and historic cultural and trading links and commitment to freedom, democracy and the rule of law. But the use of the phrase 'the special relationship' in its historical sense, to describe the totality of the ever-evolving UK-US relationship, is potentially misleading, and we recommend that its use should be avoided."<sup id="cite_ref-parl2010_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parl2010-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> In April 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> added its voice to the call for a more balanced relationship between Britain and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Cameron_and_Obama_.28May_2010.E2.80.93July_2016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cameron_and_Obama_(May_2010–July_2016)">Cameron and Obama (May 2010–July 2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cameron and Obama (May 2010–July 2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg/220px-David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg/330px-David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg/440px-David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Cameron_and_Barack_Obama_at_the_G20_Summit_in_Toronto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> (left) meets US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> (right) at the G20 Summit, June 2010.</div></div></div>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> being appointed as Prime Minister of the United Kingdom after <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_government_formation" title="2010 United Kingdom government formation">coalition talks</a> between his <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservatives</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> concluded on 11 May 2010, President Obama was the first foreign leader to offer his congratulations. Following the conversation Obama said:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>As I told the prime minister, the United States has no closer friend and ally than the United Kingdom, and I reiterated my deep and personal commitment to the special relationship between our two countries – a bond that has endured for generations and across party lines.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">William Hague</a> responded to the President's overture by making Washington his first port of call, commenting: "We're very happy to accept that description and to agree with that description. The United States is without doubt the most important ally of the United Kingdom." Meeting Hillary Clinton, Hague hailed the Special Relationship as "an unbreakable alliance", and added: "It's not a backward-looking or nostalgic relationship. It is one looking to the future from combating <a href="/wiki/Violent_extremism" title="Violent extremism">violent extremism</a> to addressing poverty and conflict around the world." Both governments confirmed their joint commitment to the war in Afghanistan and their opposition to <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran" title="Nuclear program of Iran">Iran's nuclear programme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">Deepwater Horizon oil spill</a> in 2010 sparked a media firestorm against <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a> in the United States. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">The Christian Science Monitor</a></i> observed that a "rhetorical prickliness" had come about from escalating <a href="/wiki/Obama_administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Obama administration">Obama administration</a> criticism of BP—straining the Special Relationship—particularly the repeated use of the term "British Petroleum" even though the business no longer uses that name.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Cameron stated that he did not want to make the president's toughness on BP a U.S.–U.K. issue, and noted that the company was balanced in terms of the number of its American and British shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-cameron_interview_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cameron_interview-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The validity of the Special Relationship was put in question as a result of the "aggressive rhetoric".<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 July, Cameron met with Obama during his first visit to the United States as prime minister. The two expressed unity in a wide range of issues, including the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">war in Afghanistan</a>. During the meeting, Obama stated, "We can never say it enough. The United States and the United Kingdom enjoy a truly special relationship," then going on to say, "We celebrate a common heritage. We cherish common values. ... (And) above all, our alliance thrives because it advances our common interests."<sup id="cite_ref-obama_sr_quote_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obama_sr_quote-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Cameron stated in an interview during the trip that he wanted to build a strong relationship with the United States, Britain's "oldest and best ally." This is in fact a historical error, as the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">Anglo–Portuguese Alliance</a> is the oldest alliance that is still in force. Cameron further stated that, "from the times I've met Barack Obama before, we do have very, very close – allegiances and very close positions on all the key issues, whether that is Afghanistan or Middle East peace process or Iran. Our interests are aligned and we've got to make this partnership work."<sup id="cite_ref-cameron_interview_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cameron_interview-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameron has tried to downplay the idealism of the Special Relationship and called for an end to the British fixation on the status of the relationship, stating that it's a natural and mutually beneficial relationship. He said, "...I am unapologetically pro-America. But I am not some idealistic dreamer about the special relationship. I care about the depth of our partnership, not the length of our phone calls. I hope that in the coming years we can focus on the substance, not endlessly fret about the form."<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2011, during a White House meeting with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a>, Obama declared: "We don't have a stronger friend and stronger ally than Nicolas Sarkozy, and the French people",<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> a statement which triggered outcry in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In May, however, Obama became the fourth U.S. President to make a <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visit</a> to the U.K. For the keynote speech, he became the third U.S. President to <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_addressed_both_Houses_of_the_United_Kingdom_Parliament" title="List of people who have addressed both Houses of the United Kingdom Parliament">address both Houses of Parliament</a> after <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>. Considered a rare privilege for a foreign leader, only Reagan, Clinton, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> and Nicolas Sarkozy had done so since the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP22May2011_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP22May2011-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCNews25May2011_9495513_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNews25May2011_9495513-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCNews25May2011_13533306_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNews25May2011_13533306-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> was invited to address Parliament in 2003, but declined.)<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> remarked "The relationship between the US and UK has often been described as special or essential and it has been described thus simply because it is. It was before a vote the other day in Parliament and it will be for long after that vote." This comment was brought about after the parliament vote to not conduct military strikes against Syria. <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">William Hague</a> replied: "So the United Kingdom will continue to work closely with the United States, taking a highly active role in addressing the Syria crisis and working with our closest ally over the coming weeks and months."<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Cameron stated that Obama calls him "<a href="/wiki/Brother" title="Brother">bro</a>" and described the "special relationship" between Washington and Westminster as "stronger than it has ever been".<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> In March 2016, Obama criticised the British PM for becoming "distracted" over the intervention in Libya, a criticism that was also aimed at the French President.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> A National Security Council spokesman sent an unsolicited email to the BBC limiting the damage done by stating that "Prime Minister David Cameron has been as close a partner as the president has had."<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="May_and_Obama_.28July_2016.E2.80.93January_2017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="May_and_Obama_(July_2016–January_2017)">May and Obama (July 2016–January 2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: May and Obama (July 2016–January 2017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou,_China.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou%2C_China.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou%2C_China.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou%2C_China.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou%2C_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou%2C_China.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou%2C_China.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2166" data-file-height="1452" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Theresa_May_deliver_a_joint_press_statement_in_Hangzhou,_China.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> (left) and President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> (right) deliver a joint press statement September 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The short period of relations between post-<a href="/wiki/Brexit_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="Brexit referendum">Brexit referendum</a> <a href="/wiki/2016_Conservative_Party_leadership_election" title="2016 Conservative Party leadership election">newly appointed</a> <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> and Obama administration was met with diplomatic tension over <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>'s criticism of Israel in a speech.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Obama maintained his stance that the UK would be a low priority for US trade talks post-Brexit, and that the UK would be at "the back of the queue".<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>May chose <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> to serve as her Foreign Secretary. Johnson had written an op-ed which made mention of Obama's <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenyan</a> heritage in a manner which critics accused of being racist. He had also previously written an op-ed about Hillary Clinton which made derisive statements that had been criticized as sexist.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> By the time May appointed Johnson, Clinton was the Democratic Party's presumptive nominee in <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">election to elect Obama's successor</a>, and thus had a significant chance of being the next US president. A senior official in the US government suggested that Johnson's appointment would push the US further towards <a href="/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Germany–United States relations">ties with Germany</a> at the expense of the Special Relationship with the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-ITV20160714_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITV20160714-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ultimately, before he left office, Obama stated that German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> had been his "closest international partner" throughout his tenure as President.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal2016_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal2016-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> While Obama might have had a distant relationship with Prime Minister May, he reportedly maintained a strong cordial relationship with members of the <a href="/wiki/British_royal_family" title="British royal family">British royal family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweekwed_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweekwed-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="May_and_Trump_.28January_2017.E2.80.93July_2019.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="May_and_Trump_(January_2017–July_2019)">May and Trump (January 2017–July 2019)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: May and Trump (January 2017–July 2019)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_(33998675310)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_%2833998675310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_%2833998675310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_%2833998675310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_%2833998675310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_%2833998675310%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="384" data-file-height="321" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Trump_and_Theresa_May_(33998675310)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">May</a> was the first foreign leader to visit <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Trump</a> following his inauguration.</div></div></div>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">the election</a> of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, the British government has sought to establish a close alliance with the <a href="/wiki/Trump_administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Trump administration">Trump administration</a>, which it has referred to as a revival of the historical "special relationship". May's efforts to closely associate herself with Trump have proved to be strongly controversial in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Theresa May was the first world leader to meet with President Trump following his <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_Donald_Trump" title="Inauguration of Donald Trump">inauguration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The meeting focused on post-Brexit trade, defence and security.
</p><p>Trump has reversed the stance of the Obama administration of moving the UK to the "back of queue" in regards to trade negotiations, as Trump prefers bilateral trade agreements over multilateral trade agreements, such as the proposed <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_Trade_and_Investment_Partnership" title="Transatlantic Trade and Investment Partnership">TTIP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Theresa May was criticized in the United Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-ip2_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ip2-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bi1_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bi1-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> by members of all major parties, including her own, for refusing to condemn Donald Trump's <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_13769" title="Executive Order 13769">Executive Order 13769</a>, referred to as the "Muslim ban" in the U.K.,<sup id="cite_ref-ip2_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ip2-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bi1_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bi1-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> as well as for inviting Trump to a state visit with Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McCann-Tele1Feb_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCann-Tele1Feb-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The honor of a state visit had not traditionally been extended so early in a presidency, however May did so in hopes of fostering a stronger trade relationship with the United States before the Brexit deadline.<sup id="cite_ref-visit00_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit00-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>More than 1.8&#160;million signed an official parliamentary <a href="/wiki/E-petition" class="mw-redirect" title="E-petition">e-petition</a> which said that "Donald Trump's well documented <a href="/wiki/Misogyny" title="Misogyny">misogyny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vulgarity" title="Vulgarity">vulgarity</a> disqualifies him from being received by Her Majesty the Queen or the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a>,"<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> and Opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> said in <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister%27s_Questions" title="Prime Minister&#39;s Questions">Prime Minister's Questions</a> (PMQs) that Trump should not be welcomed to Britain "while he abuses our shared values with his shameful Muslim ban and attacks on refugees' and women's rights"<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> and said that Trump should be banned from the U.K. until his travel ban is lifted.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McCann-Tele1Feb_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCann-Tele1Feb-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sayeeda_Warsi,_Baroness_Warsi" title="Sayeeda Warsi, Baroness Warsi">Baroness Warsi</a>, former chair of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservatives</a>, accused May of "bowing down" to Trump, who she described as "a man who has no respect for women, disdain for minorities, little value for LGBT communities, no compassion clearly for the vulnerable and whose policies are rooted in divisive rhetoric."<sup id="cite_ref-independent17_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent17-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> London Mayor <a href="/wiki/Sadiq_Khan" title="Sadiq Khan">Sadiq Khan</a> and the Conservative leader in Scotland, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Davidson" title="Ruth Davidson">Ruth Davidson</a>, also called for the visit to be cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent17_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent17-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Trump's invitation was later downgraded to a "working visit", in which he would not be meeting with the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite May's efforts to establish a beneficial working relationship with Trump, their relationship has been described as "dysfunctional".<sup id="cite_ref-bloombergdysfunctional_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergdysfunctional-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> It has been reported that, in their phone calls, Trump has made a habit of interrupting May.<sup id="cite_ref-bloombergdysfunctional_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergdysfunctional-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the morning of 29 November 2017, Trump <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">retweeted</a> an anti-Muslim post from the far-right group <a href="/wiki/Britain_First" title="Britain First">Britain First</a>. This received strong backlash from leaders across the British political spectrum, and was condemned by a spokesperson of May's, who said that it was, "wrong of the president to have done this."<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> Trump rebutted the statement that had been issued by May's office, Tweeting, "Don't focus on me, focus on the destructive Radical Islamic Terrorism that is taking place within the United Kingdom, We are doing just fine!"<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Trump's response to May has been seen by some as damaging to May's agenda, as it weakens the perception of a strong "special relationship" under her leadership. Thus, Trump had undone May's diligent efforts to craft an image of a close relationship with the United States in order to ease the passage of Brexit. Some have speculated that Trump's tweet might have even inflicted significant duress, if not long-term damage, to the Special Relationship itself.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The November incident would not prove to be the last time that May had to issue a condemnation of statements made by Trump offending the public of the United Kingdom, as on 5 February 2018 Trump again issued a tweet that upset many in the United Kingdom. Trump, in an attempt to rebuke a push by some in the United States' <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> to implement universal healthcare, Trump tweeted that, "thousands of people are marching in the UK because their U system is going broke and not working".<sup id="cite_ref-latimeshornets_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimeshornets-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> This was a reference the <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">healthcare</a> provided in the United Kingdom by the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a>. Trump's tweets were factually inaccurate in their characterization of the United Kingdom's health system.<sup id="cite_ref-factcheckhealth_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcheckhealth-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> mischaracterizing reasons behind recent protests in the United Kingdom (which had not been protesting <i>against</i> the universal healthcare system, but rather been protesting for an improvement in the services it offers).<sup id="cite_ref-latimeshornets_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimeshornets-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-factcheckhealth_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcheckhealth-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Trump's attack on the United Kingdom's healthcare system is believed to have placed further strain on his relationship with May, who responded by declaring her pride in the United Kingdom's health system.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independentuc_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independentuc-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 January 2018, in a televised interview with <a href="/wiki/Piers_Morgan" title="Piers Morgan">Piers Morgan</a>, Trump spoke critically of May's approach to Brexit negotiations, adding greater strain to his relationship with her.<sup id="cite_ref-independentuc_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independentuc-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/44th_G7_summit" title="44th G7 summit">2018 G7 summit</a>, Trump repeatedly made apparent slights towards May. Despite this, May stated that her relationship with Trump remained strong.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2018_Brussels_summit" title="2018 Brussels summit">2018 Brussels summit</a>, May sought to curry favor with Trump by supporting his complaints about other NATO members failing to meet certain levels of defense funding.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the Brussels summit, Trump made his first presidential visit to the United Kingdom. His visit came at period in the United Kingdom's political climate which had been preceded by significant tumult for May. She was receiving significant resistance to her plans for a "soft Brexit", which had resulted several major resignations amongst her cabinet ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytnatouk_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytnatouk-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnnsun_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnsun-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> During his visit, in an interview with <i>The Sun</i>, Trump spoke critically of May's handling of Brexit negotiations. He stated that May's proposal would likely kill the prospects of a US-UK trade agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-cnnsun_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnsun-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytnatouk_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytnatouk-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> These comments inflicted further damage on an already-embattled May.<sup id="cite_ref-nytnatouk_275-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytnatouk-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Trump also praised <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> (a political rival of May's who had recently resigned from her cabinet), going as far to suggest that Johnson would make a good prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-cnnsun_276-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnsun-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytnatouk_275-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytnatouk-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> considered that the "special relationship" had "devolved into a greasy dumpster fire" under Trump and May's coinciding periods of national leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Relations between the United Kingdom and the United States were strained after the leak of memos authored by the <a href="/wiki/British_Ambassador_to_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="British Ambassador to the United States">British Ambassador to the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Darroch" title="Kim Darroch">Kim Darroch</a>, characterizing the Trump administration as "uniquely dysfunctional" and strongly criticizing Trump's foreign policy towards <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Trump responded to the memos by claiming that Darroch "has not served the UK well" and criticizing Prime Minister May. May defended Darroch, stating that "Good government depends on public servants being able to give full and frank advice," while he was openly criticized by other British politicians such as <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Farage" title="Nigel Farage">Nigel Farage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liam_Fox" title="Liam Fox">Liam Fox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> Following Boris Johnson's refusal to defend Darroch in a debate for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Conservative_Party_leadership_election" title="2019 Conservative Party leadership election">2019 Conservative Party leadership election</a> and Trump's statements that "we will no longer deal with him," Darroch announced his resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Johnson_and_Trump_.28July_2019.E2.80.93.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Johnson_and_Trump_(July_2019–)">Johnson and Trump (July 2019–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Johnson and Trump (July 2019–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_(48616805327)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_%2848616805327%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_%2848616805327%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="337" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_%2848616805327%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_%2848616805327%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_%2848616805327%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_%2848616805327%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1042" data-file-height="1595" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johnson_and_Trump_at_the_45th_G7_in_Biarritz_-_2019_(48616805327)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister Boris Johnson (left) speaking with US President Donald Trump (right) at the <a href="/wiki/45th_G7_summit" title="45th G7 summit">45th G7 summit</a>, August 2019</div></div></div>
