<table class="box-Empty_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b> <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>It has been noted that secret defence and intelligence links "that [have] minimal impact on ordinary people [play] a disproportionate role in the transatlantic friendship",<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> and perspectives on the Special Relationship differ.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poll_findings">Poll findings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Poll findings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 1942 Gallup poll conducted after <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, before the arrival of U.S. troops and Churchill's heavy promotion of the Special Relationship, showed wartime ally <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Russia</a> was still more popular than the United States among 62% of Britons. However, only 6% had ever visited the United States and only 35% knew any Americans personally.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1969, the United States was tied with the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> as the most important overseas connection for the British public, while Europe came in a distant third. By 1984, after a decade in the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">Common Market</a>, Britons chose Europe as being most important to them.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>British opinion polls from the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(1979%E2%80%931985)" title="Cold War (1979–1985)">Cold War</a> revealed ambivalent feelings towards the United States. Margaret Thatcher's 1979 agreement to base US <a href="/wiki/Cruise_missile" title="Cruise missile">cruise missiles</a> in Britain was approved of by only 36% of Britons, and the number with little or no trust in the ability of the US to deal wisely with world affairs had soared from 38% in 1977 to 74% in 1984, by which time 49% wanted US nuclear bases in Britain removed, and 50% would have sent US-controlled cruise missiles back to the United States. At the same time, 59% of Britons supported their own country's <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nuclear weapons and the United Kingdom">nuclear deterrent</a>, with 60% believing Britain should rely on both nuclear and conventional weapons, and 66% opposing unilateral <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear disarmament</a>. 53% of Britons opposed dismantling the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/UGM-27_Polaris#British_Polaris" title="UGM-27 Polaris">Polaris</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>. 70% of Britons still considered Americans to be very or fairly trustworthy, and in case of war the United States was the ally trusted overwhelmingly to come to Britain's aid, and to risk its own security for the sake of Britain. The United States and Britain were also the two countries most alike in basic values such as willingness to fight for their country and the importance of freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1986, 71% of Britons, questioned in a Mori poll the day after Ronald Reagan's <a href="/wiki/1986_bombing_of_Libya" class="mw-redirect" title="1986 bombing of Libya">bombing of Libya</a>, disagreed with Thatcher's decision to allow the use of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> bases, while two thirds in a Gallup survey opposed the bombing itself, the reverse of US opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stop_The_War_protests_in_London,_2007-02-24.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Stop_The_War_protests_in_London%2C_2007-02-24.jpg/220px-Stop_The_War_protests_in_London%2C_2007-02-24.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Stop_The_War_protests_in_London%2C_2007-02-24.jpg/330px-Stop_The_War_protests_in_London%2C_2007-02-24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Stop_The_War_protests_in_London%2C_2007-02-24.jpg/440px-Stop_The_War_protests_in_London%2C_2007-02-24.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="686" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stop_The_War_protests_in_London,_2007-02-24.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anti-war_movement" title="Anti-war movement">Anti-war</a> protest in <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_Square" title="Trafalgar Square">Trafalgar Square</a>, February 2007</div></div></div>
<p>The United Kingdom's all-time low poll rating in the United States came in 1994, during the split over <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnia</a>, when 56% of Americans interviewed considered Britons to be close allies.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 1997 Harris poll published after Tony Blair's election, 63% of people in the United States viewed Britain as a close ally, up by one percent from 1996, 'confirming that the long-running "special relationship" with America's transatlantic cousins is still alive and well'.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> Britain came second behind its colonial offshoot Canada, on 73%, while another offshoot, Australia, came third, on 48%.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Popular awareness of the historical link was fading in the parent country, however. In a 1997 Gallup poll, while 60% of the British public said they regretted the <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">end</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Empire</a> and 70% expressed pride in the imperial past, 53% wrongly supposed that the United States had never been a <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">British possession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, 61% of Britons polled by ICM said they believed they had more in common with US citizens than they did with the rest of Europe. 64% disagreed with the sentence 'Britain does what the US government tells us to do.' A majority also backed Blair's support of Bill Clinton's strategy on <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, 42% saying action should be taken to topple <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>, with 24% favouring diplomatic action, and a further 24%, military action. A majority of Britons aged 24 and over said they did not like Blair supporting Clinton over the <a href="/wiki/Lewinsky_scandal" class="mw-redirect" title="Lewinsky scandal">Lewinsky scandal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2006 poll of the US public showed that the United Kingdom, as an 'ally in the war on terror' was viewed more positively than any other country. 76% of the US people polled viewed the British as an 'ally in the War on Terror' according to Rasmussen Reports.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> According to Harris Interactive, 74% of Americans viewed Great Britain as a 'close ally in the war in Iraq', well ahead of next-ranked Canada at 48%.
</p><p>A June 2006 poll by <a href="/wiki/Populus_Ltd" title="Populus Ltd">Populus</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> showed that the number of Britons agreeing that 'it is important for Britain's long-term security that we have a close and special relationship with America' had fallen to 58% (from 71% in April), and that 65% believed that 'Britain's future lies more with Europe than America.'<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> Only 44%, however, agreed that 'America is a force for good in the world.' A later poll during the <a href="/wiki/2006_Israel-Lebanon_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Israel-Lebanon conflict">Israel-Lebanon conflict</a> found that 63% of Britons felt that the United Kingdom was tied too closely to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> A 2008 poll by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> showed that Britons' views differed considerably from Americans' views when asked about the topics of religion, values, and national interest. <i>The Economist</i> remarked:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>For many Britons, steeped in the lore of how English-speaking democracies rallied around Britain in the second world war, [the special relationship] is something to cherish. For Winston Churchill, [...] it was a bond forged in battle. On the eve of the war in Iraq, as Britain prepared to fight alongside America, Tony Blair spoke of the 'blood price' that Britain should be prepared to pay in order to sustain the relationship.
</p><p>In America, it is not nearly as emotionally charged. Indeed American politicians are promiscuous with the term, trumpeting their 'special relationships' with Israel, Germany and South Korea, among others. 'Mention the special relationship to Americans and they say yes, it's a <i>really</i> special relationship,' notes sardonically Sir Christopher Meyer, a former British ambassador to Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>In January 2010 a Leflein poll conducted for Atlantic Bridge found that 57% of people in the US considered the special relationship with Britain to be the world's most important bilateral partnership, with 2% disagreeing. 60% of people in the US regarded Britain as the country most likely to support the United States in a crisis, while Canada came second on 24%, and Australia third on 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2010, a poll conducted in the UK by YouGov revealed that 66% of those surveyed held a favourable view of the US and 62% agreed with the assertion that America is Britain's most important ally. However, the survey also revealed that 85% of British citizens believe that the UK has little or no influence on American policies, and that 62% think that America does not consider British interests.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Another poll by YouGov in September 2016 revealed that 57% still believed in the special relationship, whilst 37% did not.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq_War">Iraq War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Iraq War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, senior British figures criticized the refusal of the <a href="/wiki/US_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="US Government">US Government</a> to heed British advice regarding post-war plans for <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, specifically the <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">Coalition Provisional Authority</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ba%27ath_Party#Post-Saddam" title="Ba&#39;ath Party">de-Ba'athification policy</a> and the critical importance of preventing the <a href="/wiki/Power_vacuum" title="Power vacuum">power vacuum</a> in which the <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">insurgency</a> subsequently developed. British defence secretary <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Hoon" title="Geoff Hoon">Geoff Hoon</a> later stated that the United Kingdom 'lost the argument' with the Bush administration over rebuilding Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extraordinary_rendition">Extraordinary rendition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Extraordinary rendition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg/220px-2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg/330px-2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg/440px-2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_09_28_rice_uk_600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> with British Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/David_Miliband" title="David Miliband">David Miliband</a>, September 2007</div></div></div>
<p>Assurances made by the United States to the United Kingdom that '<a href="/wiki/Extraordinary_rendition_by_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Extraordinary rendition by the United States">extraordinary rendition</a>' flights had never landed on British territory were later shown to be false when official US records proved that such flights had landed at Diego Garcia repeatedly.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> The revelation was an embarrassment for British foreign secretary David Miliband, who apologised to Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_law">Criminal law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Criminal law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2003, the United States pressed the United Kingdom to agree to an <a href="/wiki/Extradition_Act_2003" title="Extradition Act 2003">extradition treaty</a> which, proponents claimed, allowed for equal extradition requirements between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> Critics argued that the United Kingdom was obligated to make a strong <a href="/wiki/Prima_facie" title="Prima facie">prima facie</a> case to US courts before extradition would be granted,<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> and that, by contrast, extradition from the United Kingdom to the United States was a matter of administrative decision alone, without prima facie evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> This had been implemented as an anti-terrorist measure in the wake of 11 September 2001 attacks. Very soon, however, it was being used by the United States to extradite and prosecute a number of high-profile <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">London</a> businessmen (e.g., <a href="/wiki/The_Natwest_Three" class="mw-redirect" title="The Natwest Three">the Natwest Three</a> and Ian Norris<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup>) on fraud charges. Contrasts have been drawn with the United States' harboring of <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional IRA</a> terrorists in the 1970s through to the 1990s and repeated refusals to extradite them to the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 September 2006, the US Senate unanimously <a href="/wiki/Extradition_Act_2003#US_ratification,_2006" title="Extradition Act 2003">ratified</a> the 2003 treaty. Ratification had been slowed by complaints from some Irish-American groups that the treaty would create new legal jeopardy for US citizens who opposed British policy in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spectator" title="The Spectator">The Spectator</a></i> condemned the three-year delay as 'an appalling breach in a long-treasured relationship'.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The United States also refused to accede to another priority of the Blair government, the treaty setting-up the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_policy">Trade policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Trade policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Trade disputes and attendant job fears have sometimes strained the Special Relationship. The United States has been accused of pursuing an aggressive trade policy, using or ignoring <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a> rules; the aspects of this causing most difficulty to the United Kingdom have been a successful challenge to the protection of small family banana farmers in the West Indies from large US corporations such as the <a href="/wiki/American_Financial_Group" title="American Financial Group">American Financial Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> and high <a href="/wiki/Tariffs" class="mw-redirect" title="Tariffs">tariffs</a> on British steel products.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, Blair denounced Bush's imposition of tariffs on steel as 'unacceptable, unjustified and wrong', but although Britain's biggest steelmaker, <a href="/wiki/Corus_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Corus Group">Corus</a>, called for protection from <a href="/wiki/Dumping_(pricing_policy)" title="Dumping (pricing policy)">dumping</a> by <a href="/wiki/Developing_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing nations">developing nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_British_Industry" title="Confederation of British Industry">Confederation of British Industry</a> urged the government not to start a 'tit-for-tat'.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<table class="box-In_popular_culture plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>appears to contain <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_an_indiscriminate_collection_of_information" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">trivial, minor, or unrelated</a> references to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Trivia_sections#&quot;In_popular_culture&quot;_and_&quot;Cultural_references&quot;_material" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Trivia sections">popular culture</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please reorganize this content to explain the subject's impact on popular culture, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">providing citations</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">reliable, secondary sources</a>, rather than simply listing appearances. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table> 
<p>Over the decades, the varying <a href="/wiki/Zeitgeist" title="Zeitgeist">Zeitgeist</a> of the Special Relationship has been a feature or context or subtext for countless works of art and phenomena in <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a> as varied as <i><a href="/wiki/A_Matter_of_Life_and_Death_(film)" title="A Matter of Life and Death (film)">A Matter of Life and Death</a></i> (1946) (released as <i>Stairway to Heaven</i> in the U.S.), the <a href="/wiki/British_Invasion" title="British Invasion">British Invasion</a> of popular music beginning in the early 1960s, and the unusual intergenerational pairing of English musician <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> and American singer <a href="/wiki/Bing_Crosby" title="Bing Crosby">Bing Crosby</a> performing "<a href="/wiki/Peace_on_Earth/Little_Drummer_Boy" title="Peace on Earth/Little Drummer Boy">Peace on Earth/Little Drummer Boy</a>" in 1977.
</p><p>In the televised <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> of the 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Centauri_(Babylon_5)" title="Centauri (Babylon 5)">Centauri (Babylon 5)</a> are for plot purposes somewhat analogous to the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (July 2018)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  In the early 2000s, cultural exchange and mutual admiration between the US and UK continues, with <a href="/wiki/Masterpiece_(TV_series)" title="Masterpiece (TV series)">Masterpiece Theater</a> on <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>, including the hit series <a href="/wiki/Poldark_(2015_TV_series)" title="Poldark (2015 TV series)">Poldark</a>, and in Hollywood, with WWII-themed films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Churchill_(film)" title="Churchill (film)">Churchill</a></i> (2017), <i><a href="/wiki/Darkest_Hour_(film)" title="Darkest Hour (film)">Darkest Hour</a></i> (2017), and <i><a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_(2017_film)" title="Dunkirk (2017 film)">Dunkirk</a></i> (2017).
</p><p>A famous scene in the 2003 Christmas-themed romantic comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Actually" title="Love Actually">Love Actually</a></i> shows the British prime minister (portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Grant" title="Hugh Grant">Hugh Grant</a>) making a stand against a seemingly arrogant and intimidating US president (portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bob_Thornton" title="Billy Bob Thornton">Billy Bob Thornton</a>) during a joint press conference between the two leaders. Hugh's prime minister speaks about the need for Britain to stand up for itself more on the world stage, though within the context of the story, it's really more about the prime minister and the president fighting over the same woman, a young member of the prime minister's household staff. Nonetheless, critics regarded the scene as a commentary on then-Prime Minister Blair's supposedly obeisant stance on the US <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Existence in the 19th century and early 20th century:
<ul><li><cite class="citation news">"The Anglo-American Arbitration Treaty". <i>The Times</i>. 14 January 1897. p.&#160;5, col. C.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Times&amp;rft.atitle=The+Anglo-American+Arbitration+Treaty&amp;rft.pages=5%2C+col.+C&amp;rft.date=1897-01-14&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/>, quoting the "semi-official organ" the <i>North-German Gazette</i>: "There is, therefore, not the slightest occasion for other States to adopt as their model and example a form of agreement which may, perhaps, be advantage to England and America in their special relationship".</li>
<li><cite class="citation news">"The New American Ambassador". <i>The Times</i>. 7 June 1913. p.&#160;9, col. C.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Times&amp;rft.atitle=The+New+American+Ambassador&amp;rft.pages=9%2C+col.+C&amp;rft.date=1913-06-07&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> "No Ambassador to this or any other nation is similarly honoured ...  It is intended to be, we need hardly say, precisely what it is, a unique compliment, a recognition on our part that Great Britain and the United States stand to one another in a special relationship, and that between them some departure from the merely official attitude is most natural".</li>
<li><cite class="citation news">"The Conference and the Far East". <i>The Times</i>. 21 November 1921. p.&#160;11, col. B, C.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Times&amp;rft.atitle=The+Conference+and+the+Far+East&amp;rft.pages=11%2C+col.+B%2C+C&amp;rft.date=1921-11-21&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> "The answer of the [Japanese] Ambassador [Baron Kato] shows that he and his Government even then [1911] appreciated the special relationship between this country [the United Kingdom] and the United States ... That, probably, the Japanese Government understands now, as clearly as their predecessors understood in 1911 that we could never make war on the United States".</li>
<li><cite class="citation news">"Limit of Navy Economies". <i>The Times</i>. 13 March 1923. p.&#160;14, col. F.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Limit+of+Navy+Economies&amp;rft.pages=14%2C+col.+F&amp;rft.date=1923-03-13&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> "After comparing the programmes of Britain, America, and Japan, the First Lord said that so far from importing into our maintenance of the one-Power standard a spirit of keen and jealous competition, we had, on the contrary, interpreted it with a latitude which could only be justified by our desire to avoid provoking competition and by our conception of the special relationship of good will and mutual understanding between ourselves and the United States".</li>
<li><cite class="citation news">"Five Years Of The League". <i>The Times</i>. 10 January 1925. p.&#160;13, col. C.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Five+Years+Of+The+League&amp;rft.pages=13%2C+col.+C&amp;rft.date=1925-01-10&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> "As was well pointed out in our columns yesterday by Professor Muirhead, Great Britain stands in a quite special relationship to that great Republic [the United States]".</li>
<li><cite class="citation news">"The Walter Page Fellowships. Mr. Spender's Visit To America., Dominant Impressions". <i>The Times</i>. 23 February 1928. p.&#160;16, col. B.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Times&amp;rft.atitle=The+Walter+Page+Fellowships.+Mr.+Spender%27s+Visit+To+America.%2C+Dominant+Impressions&amp;rft.pages=16%2C+col.+B&amp;rft.date=1928-02-23&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> quoting <a href="/wiki/J._A._Spender" title="J. A. Spender">J. A. Spender</a>: "The problem for British and Americans was to make their special relationship a good relationship, to be candid and open with each other, and to refrain from the envy and uncharitableness which too often in history had embittered the dealings of kindred peoples".</li></ul>
</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-parl2010-213"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-parl2010_213-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-parl2010_213-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100401045102/http://www.parliament.uk/parliamentary_committees/foreign_affairs_committee/facpn280310.cfm">"Foreign Affairs Committee: Press Notice: Global Security: UK-US relations"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Press_release" title="Press release">Press release</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK Parliament</a>. 28 March 2010. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.parliament.uk/parliamentary_committees/foreign_affairs_committee/facpn280310.cfm">the original</a> on 1 April 2010<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 March</span> 2010</span>. <q>The UK and US have a close and valuable relationship not only in terms of intelligence and security but also in terms of our profound and historic cultural and trading links and commitment to freedom, democracy and the rule of law. But the use of the phrase 'the special relationship' in its historical sense, to describe the totality of the ever-evolving UK-US relationship, is potentially misleading, and we recommend that its use should be avoided.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Press+release&amp;rft.atitle=Foreign+Affairs+Committee%3A+Press+Notice%3A+Global+Security%3A+UK-US+relations&amp;rft.date=2010-03-28&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.parliament.uk%2Fparliamentary_committees%2Fforeign_affairs_committee%2Ffacpn280310.cfm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpecial+Relationship" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_Relationship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Arnold, Guy. <i>America and Britain: Was There Ever a Special Relationship?</i> (London: Hurst, 2014).</li>
